## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling acceleration (dv_dt) in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration typically combines nonlinear restoring forces in x, damping terms in v, and possibly periodic driving forces in t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Cubic-quintic with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Driven oscillator with quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * sin(c5 * t)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Coulomb-like damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use when oscillation is symmetric
- Even-power terms in x (x**2) break symmetry and shift the equilibrium — use when mean position drifts
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear dissipation; terms like v*x**2 represent amplitude-dependent damping
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) — check if residuals show periodic structure in t
- Negative linear stiffness (c0 > 0 for dv_dt = c0*x) combined with positive cubic term creates double-well (Duffing) potential
- If acceleration depends on v**3 or v*|v|, the system has nonlinear dissipation (Rayleigh-type or aerodynamic drag)
- Limit cycle behavior (sustained oscillations without driving) suggests Van der Pol-type terms: (1 - x**2)*v
- Softening spring behavior (amplitude-dependent frequency decrease) corresponds to negative coefficient on x**3
- Hardening spring behavior (amplitude-dependent frequency increase) corresponds to positive coefficient on x**3 when restoring coefficient is negative
